## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, so the task is to infer a kinetic rate law (an ODE right-hand side) as a function of concentration and possibly explicit time dependence (e.g., changing conditions, deactivation, forcing). With only (t, A) available, the dominant structures are standard order-based rate laws and time-varying effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or reagent-excess kinetics giving constant rate)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; exponential A(t))
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction with other species effectively tied to A)
- n-th order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global order kinetics)
- Parallel pathways (1st + 2nd order): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (competing unimolecular and bimolecular channels)
- Equilibrium relaxation (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating formation with limiting depletion/capacity)
- Self-inhibited / saturating consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by saturation or inhibition at higher A)
- Time-ramped first-order rate constant: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (temperature/programmed condition changes causing k(t))
- Exponentially decaying activity (deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate decreases with time due to catalyst decay/fouling)
- Induction/activation transient: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) (rate turns on over time via activation/wetting/mixing)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (light/chopping, oscillatory feed/temperature modulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line in dA_dt vs A), it indicates first-order kinetics with a constant effective rate constant.
- If dA_dt is nearly constant over A, it indicates zero-order kinetics and implies A(t) is approximately linear in time until depletion.
- Curvature in dA_dt vs A that steepens strongly at larger A suggests higher-than-first order terms like A**2 or A**c1.
- A mixture of linear and quadratic terms in A often reflects parallel reaction channels (e.g., unimolecular plus bimolecular loss).
- A factor of (A - c1) indicates a stable fixed point at A = c1 (relaxation toward equilibrium/steady state).
- A rational form A/(A + c1) suggests saturation or inhibition due to a limiting intermediate, site coverage, or catalyst availability.
- Explicit dependence on t in the effective rate (e.g., (c0 + c1*t) or exp(-c1*t)) indicates non-stationary conditions such as temperature ramps, catalyst deactivation, or changing mixing/transport.
- A multiplicative sinusoid in t indicates periodic external forcing (modulated irradiation, pulsed feed) imprinting oscillations on the instantaneous rate.
- Autocatalytic forms like A*(c1 - A) indicate positive feedback at low A with eventual slowdown as A approaches a limiting level.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK31)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A + c2*_w*cos(log(A + c3))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function (of feature variable **A** only; **t** unused):
\[
-0.5980340708\sqrt A\;-\;0.5980340708\,A\;+\;0.3066383448\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly**: (i) a \(\sqrt A\) term, (ii) an \(A\) term, (iii) a \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) term, and **no other nonzero functional dependence** (extra constants must be set to 0; extra terms must be removable by setting their coefficients to 0). Also, GT uses \(\sqrt A\) (not \(\sqrt{|A|}\)), and \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) (not sine with phase unless convertible).

Below, for each candidate I check whether parameters can be chosen to make it identical for all \(A\) (on the common real domain).

---

### 1. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3 + c4\sin(c5\log(Ac6+1)+c7)\)
Has sine of log, not cosine unless phase shift allowed: \(\sin(u+\pi/2)=\cos u\). So sine can represent cosine by choosing \(c7=\pi/2\) and \(c5=1\), \(c6=1\). But it also has **two independent \(A\) terms** \(Ac1+Ac2\) (can combine) and an additive constant \(c3\) (set \(c3=0\)). Then set \(c0=-0.598...\), \(c1+c2=-0.598...\), and \(c4=0.306638...\). This would match **except** the trig argument is \(\log(Ac6+1)\); with \(c6=1\) it is \(\log(A+1)\). So candidate 1 **can match**.

### 2. \(Ac0+Ac1+c2+c3\sqrt{|A|}+c4\sin(c5\log(c6|A|+1)+c7)\)
Uses \(\sqrt{|A|}\) and \(\log(c6|A|+1)\). GT uses \(\sqrt A\) and \(\log(A+1)\). These cannot be made identical for all real \(A\) (the absolute value changes the function for negative \(A\), and you cannot remove it by constants). If restricting to \(A\ge 0\), \(|A|=A\) and it could match, but equivalence “for all values” fails on reals. **No match**.

### 3. \(Ac0+c1+c2\sqrt{|A|}+c3\sin(c4\log(c5|A|+1)+c6)\)
Same absolute-value issue as (2). **No match**.

### 4. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\sin(c4\log(Ac5+1)+c6)\)
This can match: set \(c2=0\); choose sine-to-cos via \(c6=\pi/2\); set \(c4=1,c5=1\); set \(c0=-0.598...\), \(c1=-0.598...\), \(c3=0.306638...\). **Match possible**.

### 5. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\sin(c4\log(c5|A|+1)+c6)\)
Absolute value inside log breaks equality for negative \(A\). **No match**.

### 6. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + A^2c1 + A^2c2 + Ac3 + c4 + c5e^{Ac6}+c7e^{Ac8}\)
Contains \(A^2\) and exponentials; to remove them set \(c1=c2=c5=c7=0\). Then left with \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac3+c4\), but GT needs a cosine-log term. Not present. **No match**.

### 7. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2\cos(c3\log(c4|A|+1))\)
Absolute value inside log again. Also GT has \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) with no multiplicative factor inside cosine other than 1. Even if \(A\ge0\), could set \(c3=1,c4=1\), \(c2=0.306638...\), \(c0,c1\) accordingly. But for all real \(A\), **no match**.

### 8. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+Ac2+c3\cos(c4\log(c5|A|+1))\)
Same absolute value issue. **No match**.

### 9. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + A^2c1 + \sum A*ci/(A+cj) + Ac8 + c9\)
Rational terms; no trig-log cosine. Cannot generate \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). **No match**.

### 10. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + Ac1 + c2\log(Ac3+1)+c4 + c5\log(Ac6+1)/A + c7\log(Ac8+1)/A\)
Only logs and log/A; no cosine. **No match**.

### 11. Similar to (6) with \(A^2\) and exponentials; no cosine-log. **No match**.

### 12. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\cos(c4\log(Ac5+1)) + c6\exp(c7\cos(c8\log(Ac9+1)))\)
Has the needed cosine-log term, but also an extra nested exponential term. To remove it set \(c6=0\). Then set \(c2=0\), \(c4=1,c5=1\), \(c3=0.306638...\), \(c0=-0.598...\), \(c1=-0.598...\). **Match possible**.

### 13–14. Polynomial powers and \(A\log(\cdot)\); no cosine-log term. **No match**.

### 15–16. Have extra rational/exp/sin(exp) terms; can zero them, but then no cosine-log. **No match**.

### 17. Has \(\sqrt{|A|}\), sine-log, and rational term; absolute value prevents full real-line match. **No match**.

### 18. Includes \(\sqrt(A)\log(\cdot)\), logs, log/A; no cosine-log. **No match**.

### 19. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1 + A c2/(Ac3+1)+c4 + c5\sin(c6\log(Ac7+1)+c8)\)
Sine-log can become cosine-log via phase shift; set rational term off with \(c2=0\), constant \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c6=1,c7=1,c8=\pi/2\), \(c5=0.306638...\), \(c0=-0.598...\), \(c1=-0.598...\). **Match possible**.

### 20. Has only linear, logs; no cosine. **No match**.

### 21. Has \(A^2\), \(\sqrt{|A|}\), sine-log with abs; abs blocks. **No match**.

### 22–23. Linear + logs; no cosine. **No match**.

### 24–25. Include \(A^2\), exp, \(A\log\); no cosine-log. **No match**.

### 26. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\sin(c4\log(Ac5+1)+c6)+c7\log(Ac8+1)/\sqrt(A)\)
Can set \(c7=0\), \(c2=0\), and use sine phase shift to cosine. Then match as in (4). **Match possible**.

### 27–28. Rational/log/exp; no cosine-log (28 has exp*log). **No match**.

### 29. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+Ac2 + A c3/(Ac4+1)+c5 + c6\sin(c7\log(Ac8+1)+c9)\)
Set \(c3=0\), \(c5=0\), combine \(Ac1+Ac2\) to match \(-0.598...A\). Use sine→cos with \(c9=\pi/2\), \(c7=1,c8=1\), \(c6=0.306638...\), \(c0=-0.598...\). **Match possible**.

### 30–31. No cosine-log of the right form (30 has log(exp()) etc; 31 has sqrt(c5|A|+1) and log/sqrt(A)). **No match**.

### 32. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\sin(c4\log(c5|A c6|+1)+c7)\)
Absolute value inside log (via \(|A c6|\)). Breaks equality for negative \(A\). **No match**.

### 33. \(\sqrt(A)c0+Ac1+c2+c3\cos(c4\log(Ac5+1))\)

**GT:** `-0.5980*sqrt(A) - 0.5980*A + 0.3066*cos(log(A + 1))`

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Key observations about GT:**
- Terms: `c0*sqrt(A)` + `c1*A` + `c2*cos(log(A+c3))` with specific constants
- No constant offset term (when A=0: GT = 0 + 0 + 0.3066*cos(0) = 0.3066, so there IS an implicit constant contribution from the cos term)

Let me check candidates that have the right basis functions: `sqrt(A)`, `A`, and either `cos(log(...))` or `sin(log(...) + phase_shift)`.

**Candidates with sin(c*log(...) + c):**
These can match cos(log(A+1)) if the coefficient inside log is 1 and the phase shift is π/2.
